			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Teutonic Order</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">

				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the religious order. For the film, see <a href="/wiki/Knights_of_the_Teutonic_Order_(film)" title="Knights of the Teutonic Order (film)">Knights of the Teutonic Order (film)</a>.</div>

<p>The <b>Order of Brothers of the German House of Saint Mary in Jerusalem</b><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> (official names: <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <span lang="la" xml:lang="la"><i>Ordo domus Sanctæ Mariæ Theutonicorum Hierosolymitanorum</i></span>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Orden der Brüder vom Deutschen Haus der Heiligen Maria in Jerusalem</i></span>), commonly the <b>Teutonic Order</b> (<i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Deutscher Orden</span></i>, <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Deutschherrenorden</span></i> or <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Deutschritterorden</span></i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Catholic_religious_order" title="Catholic religious order">Catholic religious order</a> founded as a <a href="/wiki/Military_order_(society)" class="mw-redirect" title="Military order (society)">military order</a> c. 1190 in <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">Kingdom of Jerusalem</a>. Purely religious since 1929, it still confers limited honorary <a href="/wiki/Knighthood" class="mw-redirect" title="Knighthood">knighthoods</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The order was formed to aid <a href="/wiki/Christians" class="mw-redirect" title="Christians">Christians</a> on their <a href="/wiki/Pilgrimage" title="Pilgrimage">pilgrimages</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a> and to establish <a href="/wiki/Hospital" title="Hospital">hospitals</a>. Its members have commonly been known as the <b>Teutonic Knights</b>, having a small voluntary and <a href="/wiki/Mercenary" title="Mercenary">mercenary</a> military membership, serving as a <a href="/wiki/Crusade" class="mw-redirect" title="Crusade">crusading</a> military order for protection of Christians in the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Baltics" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltics">Baltics</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teutonic_Order&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The full name of the Order in <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> is <i>Orden der Brüder vom Deutschen Haus St. Mariens in Jerusalem</i> or in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>Ordo domus Sanctæ Mariæ Theutonicorum Hierosolymitanorum</i> (engl. "Order of the House of St. Mary of the Germans in Jerusalem"). Thus, the term 'Teutonic' refers to the German origins of the order in Latin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInnes-Parker2013102_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInnes-Parker2013102-4">[4]</a></sup> It is commonly known in German as the <i>Deutscher Orden</i> (official short name, engl. "German Order"), historically also as <i>Deutscher Ritterorden</i> ("German Order of Knights"), <i>Deutschherrenorden</i>, <i>Deutschritterorden</i> ("Order of the German Knights") or "Die Herren im weißen Mantel" ("The lords in white capes").</p>
<p>The Teutonic Knights have been known as <i>Zakon Krzyżacki</i> in <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a> ("Order of the Cross") and as <i>Kryžiuočių Ordinas</i> in <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a>, <i>Vācu Ordenis</i> in <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>, <i>Saksa Ordu</i> or, simply, <i>Ordu</i> ("The Order") in <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>, as well as various names in <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Teutonic_Knights" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:Teutonic Knights">other languages</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teutonic_Order&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Deutscher_Orden_in_Europa_1300.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Deutscher_Orden_in_Europa_1300.png/220px-Deutscher_Orden_in_Europa_1300.png" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Deutscher_Orden_in_Europa_1300.png/330px-Deutscher_Orden_in_Europa_1300.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Deutscher_Orden_in_Europa_1300.png/440px-Deutscher_Orden_in_Europa_1300.png 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1897" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Deutscher_Orden_in_Europa_1300.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Extent of the Teutonic Order in 1300.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Formed in the year 1190<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>, the medieval Order played an important role in <a href="/wiki/Outremer" title="Outremer">Outremer</a>, controlling the port tolls of Acre. After Christian forces were defeated in the Middle East, the Order moved to <a href="/wiki/Burzenland" title="Burzenland">Transylvania</a> in 1211 to help defend the South-Eastern borders of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Kipchak_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kipchak people">Kipchaks</a>. The Knights were expelled by force of arms by King <a href="/wiki/Andrew_II_of_Hungary" title="Andrew II of Hungary">Andrew II of Hungary</a> in 1225, after attempting to place themselves under <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">papal</a> instead of the original Hungarian sovereignty and thus to become independent.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1230, following the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Bull_of_Rimini" title="Golden Bull of Rimini">Golden Bull of Rimini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Master_of_the_Teutonic_Knights" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Master of the Teutonic Knights">Grand Master</a> <a href="/wiki/Hermann_von_Salza" title="Hermann von Salza">Hermann von Salza</a> and Duke <a href="/wiki/Konrad_I_of_Masovia" title="Konrad I of Masovia">Konrad I of Masovia</a> launched the <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Crusade" title="Prussian Crusade">Prussian Crusade</a>, a joint invasion of <a href="/wiki/Prussia_(region)" title="Prussia (region)">Prussia</a> intended to Christianize the Baltic <a href="/wiki/Old_Prussians" title="Old Prussians">Old Prussians</a>. The Knights had quickly taken steps against their <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Polish</a> hosts and with the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>'s support, had changed the status of <a href="/wiki/Che%C5%82mno_Land" title="Chełmno Land">Chełmno Land</a> (also Ziemia Chelminska or Kulmerland), where they were invited by the Polish prince, into their own property. Starting from there, the Order created the independent <a href="/wiki/Monastic_State_of_the_Teutonic_Knights" class="mw-redirect" title="Monastic State of the Teutonic Knights">Monastic State of the Teutonic Knights</a>, adding continuously the conquered Prussians' territory, and subsequently conquered <a href="/wiki/Livonia" title="Livonia">Livonia</a>. Over time, the kings of Poland denounced the Order for expropriating their lands, specifically Chełmno Land and later the Polish lands of <a href="/wiki/Pomerelia" title="Pomerelia">Pomerelia</a> (also Pomorze Gdańskie or Pomerania), <a href="/wiki/Kujawy" title="Kujawy">Kujawy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dobrzy%C5%84_Land" title="Dobrzyń Land">Dobrzyń Land</a>.</p>
<p>The Order theoretically lost its main purpose in Europe with the <a href="/wiki/Christianization_of_Lithuania" title="Christianization of Lithuania">Christianization of Lithuania</a>. However, it initiated numerous campaigns against its Christian neighbours, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_(1138%E2%80%931320)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Poland (1138–1320)">Kingdom of Poland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Novgorod_Republic" title="Novgorod Republic">Novgorod Republic</a> (after assimilating the <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Order" title="Livonian Order">Livonian Order</a>). The Teutonic Knights had a strong economic base which enabled them to hire mercenaries from throughout Europe to augment their feudal levies, and they also became a naval power in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>. In 1410, a Polish-Lithuanian army decisively defeated the Order and broke its military power at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grunwald" title="Battle of Grunwald">Battle of Grunwald</a> (Tannenberg). However, the capital of the Teutonic Knights was successfully defended in the following <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Marienburg_(1410)" title="Siege of Marienburg (1410)">Siege of Marienburg</a> and the Order was saved from collapse.</p>
<p>In 1515, <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor">Maximilian I</a> made a marriage alliance with <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_I_the_Old" title="Sigismund I the Old">Sigismund I</a> of Poland-Lithuania. Thereafter, the empire did not support the Order against Poland. In 1525, Grand Master <a href="/wiki/Albert,_Duke_of_Prussia" title="Albert, Duke of Prussia">Albert of Brandenburg</a> resigned and converted to <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a>, becoming <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Prussia" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke of Prussia">Duke of Prussia</a> as a vassal of Poland. Soon after, the Order lost Livonia and its holdings in the Protestant areas of Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The Order did keep its considerable holdings in Catholic areas of Germany until 1809, when <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I of France">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> ordered its dissolution and the Order lost its last secular holdings.</p>
<p>However, the Order continued to exist as a charitable and ceremonial body. It was outlawed by <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> in 1938,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> but re-established in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Today it operates primarily with charitable aims in Central Europe.</p>
<p>The Knights wore white <a href="/wiki/Surcoat" title="Surcoat">surcoats</a> with a black cross. A <a href="/wiki/Cross_patt%C3%A9e" title="Cross pattée">cross pattée</a> was sometimes used as their <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a>; this image was later used for military decoration and insignia by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a> and Germany as the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Cross" title="Iron Cross">Iron Cross</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pour_le_M%C3%A9rite" title="Pour le Mérite">Pour le Mérite</a>. The motto of the Order was: "Helfen, Wehren, Heilen" ("Help, Defend, Heal").<sup id="cite_ref-Demel_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demel-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1808px;">

</div>
</div>
</div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation">Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teutonic_Order&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1143 <a href="/wiki/Pope_Celestine_II" title="Pope Celestine II">Pope Celestine II</a> ordered the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Knights Hospitaller</a> to take over management of a German hospital in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>, which, according to the chronicler Jean d’Ypres, accommodated the countless German pilgrims and crusaders who could neither speak the local language nor Latin (<i>patriæ linguam ignorantibus atque Latinam</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Although formally an institution of the Hospitallers, the pope commanded that the prior and the brothers of the <i>domus Theutonicorum</i> (house of the Germans) should always be Germans themselves, so a tradition of a German-led religious institution could develop during the 12th century in the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">Kingdom of Jerusalem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hermann_von_Salza_Painting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Hermann_von_Salza_Painting.jpg/220px-Hermann_von_Salza_Painting.jpg" width="220" height="325" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/Hermann_von_Salza_Painting.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="443" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hermann_von_Salza_Painting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hermann_von_Salza" title="Hermann von Salza">Hermann von Salza</a> served as the fourth Grand Master of the Teutonic Knights (1209 to 1239).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the loss of Jerusalem in 1187, some merchants from <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCbeck" title="Lübeck">Lübeck</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bremen" title="Bremen">Bremen</a> took up the idea and founded a field hospital for the duration of the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Acre_(1189%E2%80%931191)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Acre (1189–1191)">Siege of Acre</a> in 1190, which became the nucleus of the order; <a href="/wiki/Celestine_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Celestine III">Celestine III</a> recognized it in 1192 by granting the monks <a href="/wiki/Augustinians" title="Augustinians">Augustinian Rule</a>. However, based on the model of the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Templar" title="Knights Templar">Knights Templar</a>, it was transformed into a military order in 1198 and the head of the order became known as the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Master_of_the_Teutonic_Knights" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Master of the Teutonic Knights">Grand Master</a> (<i>magister hospitalis</i>). It received <a href="/wiki/Papacy" class="mw-redirect" title="Papacy">papal</a> orders for crusades to take and hold Jerusalem for <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> and defend the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a> against the Muslim <a href="/wiki/Saracen" title="Saracen">Saracens</a>. During the rule of Grand Master <a href="/wiki/Hermann_von_Salza" title="Hermann von Salza">Hermann von Salza</a> (1209–1239) the Order changed from being a <a href="/wiki/Palliative_care" title="Palliative care">hospice</a> brotherhood for pilgrims to primarily a military order.</p>
<p>The Order was founded in Acre, and the Knights purchased <a href="/wiki/Montfort_(castle)" class="mw-redirect" title="Montfort (castle)">Montfort (Starkenberg)</a>, northeast of Acre, in 1220. This castle, which defended the route between Jerusalem and the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>, was made the seat of the Grand Masters in 1229, although they returned to Acre after losing Montfort to Muslim control in 1271. The Order also had a castle at <a href="/wiki/Amouda" title="Amouda">Amouda</a> in <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Kingdom_of_Cilicia" title="Armenian Kingdom of Cilicia">Armenia Minor</a>. The Order received donations of land in the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> (especially in present-day Germany and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>), <a href="/wiki/Frankish_Greece" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankish Greece">Frankish Greece</a>, and the Kingdom of Jerusalem.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick II</a> elevated his close friend Hermann von Salza to the status of <i><a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCrst" title="Fürst">Reichsfürst</a></i>, or "Prince of the Empire", enabling the Grand Master to negotiate with other senior princes as an equal. During Frederick's coronation as <a href="/wiki/King_of_Jerusalem" title="King of Jerusalem">King of Jerusalem</a> in 1225, Teutonic Knights served as his escort in the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre" title="Church of the Holy Sepulchre">Church of the Holy Sepulchre</a>; von Salza read the emperor's proclamation in both French and <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>. However, the Teutonic Knights were never as influential in <a href="/wiki/Outremer" title="Outremer">Outremer</a> as the older Templars and Hospitallers.</p>
<h3><span id="Transylvania,_Kingdom_of_Hungary"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Transylvania.2C_Kingdom_of_Hungary">Transylvania, Kingdom of Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teutonic_Order&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Transylvania, Kingdom of Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Codex_Manesse_Tannh%C3%A4user.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Codex_Manesse_Tannh%C3%A4user.jpg/220px-Codex_Manesse_Tannh%C3%A4user.jpg" width="220" height="323" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Codex_Manesse_Tannh%C3%A4user.jpg/330px-Codex_Manesse_Tannh%C3%A4user.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Codex_Manesse_Tannh%C3%A4user.jpg/440px-Codex_Manesse_Tannh%C3%A4user.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1007" data-file-height="1478" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Codex_Manesse_Tannh%C3%A4user.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tannh%C3%A4user" title="Tannhäuser">Tannhäuser</a> in the habit of the Teutonic Knights, from the <i><a href="/wiki/Codex_Manesse" title="Codex Manesse">Codex Manesse</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1211, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_II_of_Hungary" title="Andrew II of Hungary">Andrew II</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Hungary</a> accepted the services of the Teutonic Knights and granted them the district of <a href="/wiki/Burzenland" title="Burzenland">Burzenland</a> in <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>. Andrew had been involved in negotiations for the marriage of his daughter with the son of Hermann, Landgrave of <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a>, whose vassals included the family of Hermann von Salza. Led by a brother called Theoderich, the Order defended the South-Eastern borders of the Kingdom of Hungary against the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Cumans" title="Cumans">Cumans</a>. They settled new Germans among the existing inhabitants, who were known as the <a href="/wiki/Transylvanian_Saxons" title="Transylvanian Saxons">Transylvanian Saxons</a>. In 1224, the Knights petitioned <a href="/wiki/Pope_Honorius_III" title="Pope Honorius III">Pope Honorius III</a> to be placed directly under the authority of the <a href="/wiki/Papal_See" class="mw-redirect" title="Papal See">Papal See</a>, rather than that of the King of Hungary. Angered and alarmed at their growing power, Andrew responded by expelling them in 1225, although he allowed the new arrivals to remain.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prussia">Prussia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teutonic_Order&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Prussia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Crusade" title="Prussian Crusade">Prussian Crusade</a></div>
<p>In 1226, <a href="/wiki/Konrad_I_of_Masovia" title="Konrad I of Masovia">Konrad I</a>, Duke of <a href="/wiki/Masovia" class="mw-redirect" title="Masovia">Masovia</a> in north-eastern <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, appealed to the Knights to defend his borders and subdue the pagan Baltic <a href="/wiki/Prussian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Prussian people">Prussians</a>, allowing the Teutonic Knights use of <a href="/wiki/Che%C5%82mno_Land" title="Chełmno Land">Chełmno Land</a> (Culmerland) as a base for their campaign. This being a time of widespread crusading fervor throughout Western Europe, Hermann von Salza considered <a href="/wiki/Prussia_(region)" title="Prussia (region)">Prussia</a> a good training ground for his knights for the wars against the <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> in <a href="/wiki/Outremer" title="Outremer">Outremer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> With the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Bull_of_Rimini" title="Golden Bull of Rimini">Golden Bull of Rimini</a>, Emperor Frederick II bestowed on the Order a special imperial privilege for the conquest and possession of Prussia, including Chełmno Land, with nominal papal sovereignty. In 1235 the Teutonic Knights assimilated the smaller <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Dobrzy%C5%84" title="Order of Dobrzyń">Order of Dobrzyń</a>, which had been established earlier by <a href="/wiki/Christian_of_Oliva" title="Christian of Oliva">Christian</a>, the first Bishop of Prussia.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_Janssen,_Kaiser_Friedrich_II.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Peter_Janssen%2C_Kaiser_Friedrich_II.jpg/220px-Peter_Janssen%2C_Kaiser_Friedrich_II.jpg" width="220" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Peter_Janssen%2C_Kaiser_Friedrich_II.jpg/330px-Peter_Janssen%2C_Kaiser_Friedrich_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8b/Peter_Janssen%2C_Kaiser_Friedrich_II.jpg 2x" data-file-width="369" data-file-height="366" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_Janssen,_Kaiser_Friedrich_II.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick II</a> allows the order to invade Prussia</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Janssen" title="Peter Janssen">P. Janssen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Prussia" class="mw-redirect" title="Conquest of Prussia">conquest of Prussia</a> was accomplished with much bloodshed over more than fifty years, during which native Prussians who remained unbaptised were subjugated, killed, or exiled. Fighting between the Knights and the Prussians was ferocious; chronicles of the Order state the Prussians would "roast captured brethren alive in their armour, like chestnuts, before the shrine of a local god".<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> [citation needed]</p>
<p>The native nobility who submitted to the crusaders had many of their privileges affirmed in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Christburg" title="Treaty of Christburg">Treaty of Christburg</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Prussian_uprisings" title="Prussian uprisings">Prussian uprisings</a> of 1260–83, however, much of the Prussian nobility emigrated or were resettled, and many free Prussians lost their rights. The Prussian nobles who remained were more closely allied with the German landowners and gradually assimilated.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Peasants in frontier regions, such as <a href="/wiki/Sambia_Peninsula" title="Sambia Peninsula">Samland</a>, had more privileges than those in more populated lands, such as <a href="/wiki/Pomesania" class="mw-redirect" title="Pomesania">Pomesania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The crusading knights often accepted <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">baptism</a> as a form of submission by the natives.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Christianity along western lines slowly spread through Prussian culture. Bishops were reluctant to have Prussian religious practices integrated into the new faith,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> while the ruling knights found it easier to govern the natives when they were semi-pagan and lawless.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> After fifty years of warfare and brutal conquest, the end result meant that most of the Prussian natives were either killed or deported.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Teutonic_Order_1260.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Teutonic_Order_1260.png/220px-Teutonic_Order_1260.png" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Teutonic_Order_1260.png/330px-Teutonic_Order_1260.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Teutonic_Order_1260.png/440px-Teutonic_Order_1260.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1043" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Teutonic_Order_1260.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the Teutonic state in 1260</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Order ruled Prussia under <a href="/wiki/Golden_Bull_of_Rimini" title="Golden Bull of Rimini">charters</a> issued by the Pope and the Holy Roman Emperor as a <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereign</a> <a href="/wiki/Monastic_state_of_the_Teutonic_Knights" class="mw-redirect" title="Monastic state of the Teutonic Knights">monastic state</a>, comparable to the arrangement of the Knights Hospitallers in <a href="/wiki/Rhodes" title="Rhodes">Rhodes</a> and later in <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>.</p>
<p>To make up for losses from the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">plague</a> and to replace the partially exterminated native population, the Order encouraged <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a> from the Holy Roman Empire (mostly <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flemish_people" title="Flemish people">Flemish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>) and from Masovia (<a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>), the later <a href="/wiki/Masurians" title="Masurians">Masurians</a>. These included nobles, burghers, and peasants, and the surviving Old Prussians were gradually assimilated through <a href="/wiki/Germanization" class="mw-redirect" title="Germanization">Germanization</a>. The settlers founded numerous towns and cities on former Prussian settlements. The Order itself built a number of castles (<i><a href="/wiki/Ordensburg" title="Ordensburg">Ordensburgen</a></i>) from which it could defeat <a href="/wiki/Prussian_uprisings" title="Prussian uprisings">uprisings of Old Prussians</a>, as well as continue its attacks on the Grand Duchy of Lithuania and the Kingdom of Poland, with which the Order was often at war during the 14th and 15th centuries. Major towns founded by the Order included <a href="/wiki/Olsztyn" title="Olsztyn">Allenstein (Olsztyn)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elbl%C4%85g" title="Elbląg">Elbing (Elbląg)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da" title="Klaipėda">Klaipėda (Memel)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsberg" title="Königsberg">Königsberg</a>, founded in 1255 in honor of King <a href="/wiki/Otakar_II_of_Bohemia" class="mw-redirect" title="Otakar II of Bohemia">Otakar II</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a> on the site of a destroyed Prussian settlement.</p>
<p>In 1236 the <a href="/wiki/Knights_of_Saint_Thomas" title="Knights of Saint Thomas">Knights of Saint Thomas</a>, an English order, adopted the rules of the Teutonic Order. A contingent of Teutonic Knights of indeterminate number is traditionally believed to have participated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Legnica" title="Battle of Legnica">Battle of Legnica</a> in 1241 against the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe" title="Mongol invasion of Europe">Mongols</a>. However, recent analysis of the 15th century <i>Annals of Jan Długosz</i> by Labuda suggests that the German crusaders may have been added to the text (listing the Allied Army) after the chronicler <a href="/wiki/Jan_D%C5%82ugosz" title="Jan Długosz">Długosz</a> had completed the work.<sup id="cite_ref-Empires_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Empires-21">[21]</a></sup> Legnica is the furthest west the Mongol expansion would reach in Poland.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Livonia">Livonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teutonic_Order&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Livonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Crusade" title="Livonian Crusade">Livonian Crusade</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paide_ordulinnuse_varemed_2013.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Teutonic Order castle in Paide, Estonia." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Paide_ordulinnuse_varemed_2013.JPG/220px-Paide_ordulinnuse_varemed_2013.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Paide_ordulinnuse_varemed_2013.JPG/330px-Paide_ordulinnuse_varemed_2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Paide_ordulinnuse_varemed_2013.JPG/440px-Paide_ordulinnuse_varemed_2013.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4512" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paide_ordulinnuse_varemed_2013.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Teutonic Order castle in <a href="/wiki/Paide" title="Paide">Paide</a>, Estonia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Brothers_of_the_Sword" title="Livonian Brothers of the Sword">Livonian Brothers of the Sword</a> were absorbed by the Teutonic Knights in 1237, after the former had suffered a devastating defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Saule" title="Battle of Saule">Battle of Saule</a>. The Livonian branch subsequently became known as the <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Order" title="Livonian Order">Livonian Order</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Plakans_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plakans-22">[22]</a></sup> Attempts to expand into Kievan Rus failed when the knights suffered a major defeat in 1242 in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Ice" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of the Ice">Battle of the Ice</a> at the hands of Prince <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky" title="Alexander Nevsky">Alexander Nevsky</a> of <a href="/wiki/Novgorod_Republic" title="Novgorod Republic">Novgorod</a>. Over the next decades the Order focused on the subjugation of the <a href="/wiki/Curonians" title="Curonians">Curonians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semigallians" title="Semigallians">Semigallians</a>. In 1260 it suffered a disastrous defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Durbe" title="Battle of Durbe">Battle of Durbe</a> against <a href="/wiki/Samogitians" title="Samogitians">Samogitians</a>, which inspired rebellions throughout Prussia and Livonia. After the Teutonic Knights won a crucial victory in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_K%C3%B6nigsberg" title="Siege of Königsberg">Siege of Königsberg</a> from 1262 to 1265, the war had reached a turning point. The Curonians were finally subjugated in 1267 and the Semigallians in 1290.<sup id="cite_ref-Plakans_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plakans-22">[22]</a></sup> The Order suppressed a <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Night_Uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="St. George's Night Uprising">major Estonian rebellion</a> in 1343-1345, and in 1346 purchased the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Estonia#Duchy_of_Estonia" title="Danish Estonia">Duchy of Estonia</a> from <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Against_Lithuania">Against Lithuania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teutonic_Order&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Against Lithuania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Teutonic Knights began to direct their campaigns against pagan <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Lithuania</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_mythology" title="Lithuanian mythology">Lithuanian mythology</a>), due to the aim to have all the world be <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a>, especially after the fall of the Kingdom of Jerusalem at Acre in 1291. The knights moved their headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, from which they planned the recovery of Outremer.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Because "<a href="/wiki/Lithuania_proper" title="Lithuania proper">Lithuania Propria</a>" remained non-Christian until the end of the 14th century, much later than the rest of eastern Europe, many knights from western European countries, such as England and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, journeyed to Prussia to participate in the seasonal campaigns (<i>reyse</i>) against the Grand Duchy of Lithuania. Some of them campaigned against pagans to obtain remission for their sins, while others fought to gain military experience. In 1348, the Order won a great victory over the Lithuanians in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Str%C4%97va" title="Battle of Strėva">Battle of Strėva</a>, severely weakening them. The Teutonic Knights won a decisive victory over Lithuania in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Rudau" title="Battle of Rudau">Battle of Rudau</a> in 1370.</p>
<p>Warfare between the Order and the Lithuanians was especially brutal. Non-Christians were seen as lacking rights possessed by Christians. Because enslavement of non-Christians was seen as acceptable at the time and the subdued native Prussians demanded land or payment, the Knights often used captured pagan Lithuanians for forced labor. The contemporary <a href="/wiki/Archduchy_of_Austria" title="Archduchy of Austria">Austrian</a> poet Peter Suchenwirt described treatment he witnessed of pagans by the Knights:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Women and children were taken captive; What a jolly medley could be seen: Many a woman could be seen, Two children tied to her body, One behind and one in front; On a horse without spurs Barefoot had they ridden here; The heathens were made to suffer: Many were captured and in every case, Were their hands tied together They were led off, all tied up&#160;— Just like hunting dogs.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>It was a total war in every sense of the word, lasting over 200 years, with its front line along both banks of the <a href="/wiki/Neman_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Neman River">Neman River</a>, with as many as twenty forts and castles between <a href="/wiki/Sered%C5%BEius" title="Seredžius">Seredžius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jurbarkas" title="Jurbarkas">Jurbarkas</a> alone, creating an absolutely desolated wasteland. This struggle was so deeply etched into <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Lithuania" title="Culture of Lithuania">Lithuanian culture</a> and mentality that even now it is a prominent source of national pride and self-identity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Against_Poland">Against Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teutonic_Order&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Against Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_takeover_of_Danzig" class="mw-redirect" title="Teutonic takeover of Danzig">Teutonic takeover of Danzig</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pommerellen.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Pommerellen.png/220px-Pommerellen.png" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f2/Pommerellen.png 1.5x" data-file-width="288" data-file-height="226" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pommerellen.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pomerelia (<i>Pommerellen</i>) while part of the <a href="/wiki/Monastic_state_of_the_Teutonic_Knights" class="mw-redirect" title="Monastic state of the Teutonic Knights">monastic state of the Teutonic Knights</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A dispute over the succession to the Duchy of <a href="/wiki/Pomerelia" title="Pomerelia">Pomerelia</a> embroiled the Order in further conflict at the beginning of the 14th century. The Margraves of <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a> had claims to the duchy that they acted upon after the death of King <a href="/wiki/Wenceslaus_III_of_Bohemia" title="Wenceslaus III of Bohemia">Wenceslaus</a> of Poland in 1306. Duke <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_I_the_Elbow-high" title="Władysław I the Elbow-high">Władysław I the Elbow-high</a> of Poland also claimed the duchy, based on inheritance from <a href="/wiki/Przemys%C5%82_II" title="Przemysł II">Przemysław II</a>, but he was opposed by some <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomeranians</a> nobles. They requested help from Brandenburg, which subsequently occupied all of Pomerelia except for the citadel of Danzig (<a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gdańsk">Gdańsk</a>) in 1308. Because Władysław was unable to come to the defense of Danzig, the Teutonic Knights, then led by Hochmeister <a href="/wiki/Siegfried_von_Feuchtwangen" title="Siegfried von Feuchtwangen">Siegfried von Feuchtwangen</a>, were hired to expel the Brandenburgers.</p>
<p>The Order, under Prussian Landmeister <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_von_Pl%C3%B6tzke" title="Heinrich von Plötzke">Heinrich von Plötzke</a>, evicted the Brandenburgers from Danzig in September 1308 but then refused to yield the town to the Poles and <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_takeover_of_Danzig_(Gda%C5%84sk)" title="Teutonic takeover of Danzig (Gdańsk)">massacred the town's inhabitants</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Soldin_(1309)" title="Treaty of Soldin (1309)">Treaty of Soldin</a>, the Teutonic Order purchased Brandenburg's supposed claim to the castles of Danzig, Schwetz (<a href="/wiki/%C5%9Awiecie" title="Świecie">Świecie</a>), and Dirschau (<a href="/wiki/Tczew" title="Tczew">Tczew</a>) and their hinterlands from the margraves for 10,000 marks on 13 September 1309.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Control of Pomerelia allowed the Order to connect their monastic state with the borders of the Holy Roman Empire. Crusading reinforcements and supplies could travel from the Imperial territory of <a href="/wiki/Hither_Pomerania" class="mw-redirect" title="Hither Pomerania">Hither Pomerania</a> through Pomerelia to Prussia, while Poland's access to the Baltic Sea was blocked. While Poland had mostly been an ally of the knights against the pagan Prussians and Lithuanians, the capture of Pomerelia turned the kingdom into a determined enemy of the Order.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The capture of Danzig marked a new phase in the history of the Teutonic Knights. The persecution and abolition of the powerful Knights Templar, which began in 1307, worried the Teutonic Knights, but control of Pomerelia allowed them to move their headquarters in 1309 from Venice to <a href="/wiki/Malbork" title="Malbork">Marienburg (Malbork)</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Nogat_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Nogat River">Nogat River</a>, outside the reach of secular powers. The position of Prussian Landmeister was merged with that of the Grand Master. The Pope began investigating misconduct by the knights, but the Order was defended by able jurists. Along with the campaigns against the Lithuanians, the knights faced a vengeful Poland and legal threats from the Papacy.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Kalisz_(1343)" title="Treaty of Kalisz (1343)">Treaty of Kalisz of 1343</a> ended open war between the Teutonic Knights and Poland. The Knights relinquished <a href="/wiki/Kuyavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuyavia">Kuyavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dobrzy%C5%84_Land" title="Dobrzyń Land">Dobrzyń Land</a> to Poland, but retained <a href="/wiki/Che%C5%82mno_Land" title="Chełmno Land">Culmerland</a> and Pomerelia with Danzig.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Height_of_power">Height of power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teutonic_Order&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Height of power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Teutonic_Order_1410.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Teutonic_Order_1410.png/220px-Teutonic_Order_1410.png" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Teutonic_Order_1410.png/330px-Teutonic_Order_1410.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Teutonic_Order_1410.png/440px-Teutonic_Order_1410.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1043" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Teutonic_Order_1410.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the Teutonic state in 1410</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1337, Emperor <a href="/wiki/Louis_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Louis IV, Holy Roman Emperor">Louis IV</a> allegedly granted the Order the imperial privilege to conquer all Lithuania and Russia. During the reign of Grand Master <a href="/wiki/Winrich_von_Kniprode" title="Winrich von Kniprode">Winrich von Kniprode</a> (1351–1382), the Order reached the peak of its international prestige and hosted numerous European crusaders and nobility.</p>
<p>King <a href="/wiki/Albert_of_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="Albert of Sweden">Albert</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> ceded <a href="/wiki/Gotland" title="Gotland">Gotland</a> to the Order as a pledge (similar to a <a href="/wiki/Fiefdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiefdom">fiefdom</a>), with the understanding that they would eliminate the pirating <a href="/wiki/Victual_Brothers" title="Victual Brothers">Victual Brothers</a> from this strategic island base in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>. An invasion force under Grand Master <a href="/wiki/Konrad_von_Jungingen" class="mw-redirect" title="Konrad von Jungingen">Konrad von Jungingen</a> conquered the island in 1398 and drove the Victual Brothers out of Gotland and the Baltic Sea.</p>
<p>In 1386, Grand Duke <a href="/wiki/Jogaila" class="mw-redirect" title="Jogaila">Jogaila</a> of Lithuania was <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">baptised</a> into Christianity and married Queen <a href="/wiki/Jadwiga_of_Poland" title="Jadwiga of Poland">Jadwiga of Poland</a>, taking the name Władysław II Jagiełło and becoming King of Poland. This created a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> between the two countries and a potentially formidable opponent for the Teutonic Knights. The Order initially managed to play Jagiello and his cousin <a href="/wiki/Vytautas_the_Great" class="mw-redirect" title="Vytautas the Great">Vytautas</a> against each other, but this strategy failed when Vytautas began to suspect that the Order was planning to annex parts of his territory.</p>
<p>The baptism of Jagiello began the official conversion of Lithuania to Christianity. Although the crusading rationale for the Order's state ended when Prussia and Lithuania had become officially Christian, the Order's feuds and wars with Lithuania and Poland continued. The <a href="/wiki/Lizard_Union_(medieval)" title="Lizard Union (medieval)">Lizard Union</a> was created in 1397 by Prussian nobles in Culmerland to oppose the Order's policy.</p>
<p>In 1407, the Teutonic Order reached its greatest territorial extent and included the lands of <a href="/wiki/Prussia_(region)" title="Prussia (region)">Prussia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pomerelia" title="Pomerelia">Pomerelia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samogitia" title="Samogitia">Samogitia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Courland" title="Courland">Courland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Livonia" title="Livonia">Livonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gotland" title="Gotland">Gotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hiiumaa" title="Hiiumaa">Dagö</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saaremaa" title="Saaremaa">Ösel</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Neumark" title="Neumark">Neumark</a>, pawned by Brandenburg in 1402.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline">Decline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teutonic_Order&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Decline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jan_Matejko,_Bitwa_pod_Grunwaldem.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Jan_Matejko%2C_Bitwa_pod_Grunwaldem.jpg/220px-Jan_Matejko%2C_Bitwa_pod_Grunwaldem.jpg" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Jan_Matejko%2C_Bitwa_pod_Grunwaldem.jpg/330px-Jan_Matejko%2C_Bitwa_pod_Grunwaldem.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Jan_Matejko%2C_Bitwa_pod_Grunwaldem.jpg/440px-Jan_Matejko%2C_Bitwa_pod_Grunwaldem.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3571" data-file-height="1553" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jan_Matejko,_Bitwa_pod_Grunwaldem.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Battle of Grunwald</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Jan_Matejko" title="Jan Matejko">Jan Matejko</a> (1878)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1410, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grunwald" title="Battle of Grunwald">Battle of Grunwald</a> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Schlacht bei Tannenberg</i></span>)&#160;— known in Lithuanian as the Battle of Žalgiris&#160;— a combined Polish-Lithuanian army, led by <a href="/wiki/Vytautas" title="Vytautas">Vytautas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jogaila" class="mw-redirect" title="Jogaila">Jogaila</a>, decisively defeated the Order in the <a href="/wiki/Polish-Lithuanian-Teutonic_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish-Lithuanian-Teutonic War">Polish-Lithuanian-Teutonic War</a>. Grand Master <a href="/wiki/Ulrich_von_Jungingen" title="Ulrich von Jungingen">Ulrich von Jungingen</a> and most of the Order's higher dignitaries fell on the battlefield (50 out of 60). The Polish-Lithuanian army then began the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Marienburg_(1410)" title="Siege of Marienburg (1410)">Siege of Marienburg</a>, the capital of the Order, but was unable to take <a href="/wiki/Malbork_castle" class="mw-redirect" title="Malbork castle">Marienburg</a> owing to the resistance of <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_von_Plauen" title="Heinrich von Plauen">Heinrich von Plauen</a>. When the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Thorn_(1411)" title="Peace of Thorn (1411)">First Peace of Thorn</a> was signed in 1411, the Order managed to retain essentially all of its territories, although the Knights' reputation as invincible warriors was irreparably damaged.</p>
<p>While Poland and Lithuania were growing in power, that of the Teutonic Knights dwindled through infighting. They were forced to impose high taxes to pay a substantial indemnity but did not give the cities sufficient requested representation in the administration of their state. The authoritarian and reforming Grand Master Heinrich von Plauen was forced from power and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Michael_K%C3%BCchmeister_von_Sternberg" title="Michael Küchmeister von Sternberg">Michael Küchmeister von Sternberg</a>, but the new Grand Master was unable to revive the Order's fortunes. After the <a href="/wiki/Gollub_War" title="Gollub War">Gollub War</a> the Knights lost some small border regions and renounced all claims to <a href="/wiki/Samogitia" title="Samogitia">Samogitia</a> in the 1422 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Melno" title="Treaty of Melno">Treaty of Melno</a>. <a href="/wiki/Austrians" title="Austrians">Austrian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bavarians" title="Bavarians">Bavarian</a> knights feuded with those from the <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a>, who likewise bickered with <a href="/wiki/Low_German" title="Low German">Low German</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a>, from whose ranks the Grand Master was usually chosen. The western Prussian lands of the <a href="/wiki/Vistula" title="Vistula">Vistula</a> River Valley and the Brandenburg Neumark were ravaged by the <a href="/wiki/Hussite" class="mw-redirect" title="Hussite">Hussites</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Hussite_Wars" title="Hussite Wars">Hussite Wars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Some Teutonic Knights were sent to battle the invaders, but were defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemian</a> infantry. The Knights also sustained a defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Polish-Teutonic_War_(1431-1435)" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish-Teutonic War (1431-1435)">Polish-Teutonic War (1431-1435)</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Teutonic_Order_1466.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Teutonic_Order_1466.png/220px-Teutonic_Order_1466.png" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Teutonic_Order_1466.png/330px-Teutonic_Order_1466.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Teutonic_Order_1466.png/440px-Teutonic_Order_1466.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1043" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Teutonic_Order_1466.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the Teutonic state in 1466</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1454, the <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Confederation" title="Prussian Confederation">Prussian Confederation</a>, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Gentry" title="Gentry">gentry</a> and burghers of western Prussia, rose up against the Order, beginning the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Years%27_War_(1454%E2%80%9366)" title="Thirteen Years' War (1454–66)">Thirteen Years' War</a>. Much of Prussia was devastated in the war, during the course of which the Order returned Neumark to Brandenburg in 1455. In the <a href="/wiki/Second_Peace_of_Thorn_(1466)" title="Second Peace of Thorn (1466)">Second Peace of Thorn (1466)</a>, the defeated Order recognized the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poland_(1385%E2%80%931569)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Poland (1385–1569)">Polish crown</a>'s rights over western Prussia (subsequently <a href="/wiki/Royal_Prussia" title="Royal Prussia">Royal Prussia</a>) while retaining eastern Prussia under nominal Polish overlordship. Because Marienburg Castle was handed over to mercenaries in lieu of their pay, the Order moved its base to <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsberg" title="Königsberg">Königsberg</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sambia_Peninsula" title="Sambia Peninsula">Sambia</a>.</p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Teutonic_War_(1519%E2%80%931521)" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish–Teutonic War (1519–1521)">Polish–Teutonic War (1519–1521)</a>, the Order was completely ousted from Prussia when Grand Master <a href="/wiki/Albert_I,_Duke_of_Prussia" class="mw-redirect" title="Albert I, Duke of Prussia">Albert of Brandenburg</a> converted to <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> in 1525. He secularized the Order's remaining Prussian territories and assumed from his uncle <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_I_the_Old" title="Sigismund I the Old">Sigismund I the Old</a>, King of Poland, the hereditary rights to the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Prussia" title="Duchy of Prussia">Duchy of Prussia</a> as a vassal of the Polish Crown, the <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Homage" title="Prussian Homage">Prussian Homage</a>. The Protestant Duchy of Prussia was thus a fief of Catholic Poland.</p>
<p>Although it had lost control of all of its Prussian lands, the Teutonic Order retained its territories within the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Livonia" title="Livonia">Livonia</a>, although the Livonian branch retained considerable autonomy. Many of the Imperial possessions were ruined in the <a href="/wiki/German_Peasants%27_War" title="German Peasants' War">German Peasants' War</a> from 1524 to 1525 and subsequently confiscated by Protestant territorial princes.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The Livonian territory was then partitioned by neighboring powers during the <a href="/wiki/Livonian_War" title="Livonian War">Livonian War</a>; in 1561 the Livonian Master <a href="/wiki/Gotthard_Kettler" title="Gotthard Kettler">Gotthard Kettler</a> secularized the southern Livonian possessions of the Order to create the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Courland" class="mw-redirect" title="Duchy of Courland">Duchy of Courland</a>, also a vassal of Poland.</p>
<p>After the loss of Prussia in 1525, the Teutonic Knights concentrated on their possessions in the Holy Roman Empire. Since they held no contiguous territory, they developed a three-tiered administrative system: holdings were combined into <a href="/wiki/Commandry_(feudalism)" class="mw-redirect" title="Commandry (feudalism)">commanderies</a> that were administered by a <a href="/wiki/Komtur" class="mw-redirect" title="Komtur">commander</a> (<i>Komtur</i>). Several commanderies were combined to form a <a href="/wiki/Bailiwick" title="Bailiwick">bailiwick</a> headed by a <i>Landkomtur</i>. All of the Teutonic Knights' possessions were subordinate to the Grand Master, whose seat was in Bad Mergentheim.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Badmgh_schloss_seite.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Badmgh_schloss_seite.jpg/220px-Badmgh_schloss_seite.jpg" width="220" height="367" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Badmgh_schloss_seite.jpg/330px-Badmgh_schloss_seite.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Badmgh_schloss_seite.jpg/440px-Badmgh_schloss_seite.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2726" data-file-height="4544" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Badmgh_schloss_seite.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Castle of the Teutonic Order in <a href="/wiki/Bad_Mergentheim" title="Bad Mergentheim">Bad Mergentheim</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There were twelve German bailiwicks:</p>
<ul>
<li>Thuringia;</li>
<li>Alden Biesen (in present-day <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>);</li>
<li>Hesse;</li>
<li>Saxony;</li>
<li>Westphalia;</li>
<li>Franconia;</li>
<li>Koblenz;</li>
<li>Alsace-Burgundy;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/An_der_Etsch" title="An der Etsch">An der Etsch und im Gebirge</a> (in <a href="/wiki/County_of_Tyrol" title="County of Tyrol">Tyrol</a>);</li>
<li>Utrecht;</li>
<li>Lorraine; and</li>
<li>Austria.</li>
</ul>
<p>Outside of German areas were the bailiwicks of</p>
<ul>
<li>Sicily;</li>
<li>Apulia;</li>
<li>Lombardy;</li>
<li>Bohemia;</li>
<li>"Romania" (in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>); and</li>
<li>Armenia-Cyprus.</li>
</ul>
<p>The Order gradually lost control of these holdings until, by 1810, only the bailiwicks in Tyrol and Austria remained.</p>
<p>Following the abdication of Albert of Brandenburg, <a href="/wiki/Walter_von_Cronberg" title="Walter von Cronberg">Walter von Cronberg</a> became <i>Deutschmeister</i> in 1527, and later Administrator of Prussia and Grand Master in 1530. Emperor <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a> combined the two positions in 1531, creating the title <i>Hoch- und Deutschmeister</i>, which also had the rank of <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCrst" title="Fürst">Prince of the Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> A new Grand Magistery was established in Mergentheim in <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Württemberg">Württemberg</a>, which was attacked during the German Peasants' War. The Order also helped Charles V against the <a href="/wiki/Schmalkaldic_League" title="Schmalkaldic League">Schmalkaldic League</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Augsburg" title="Peace of Augsburg">Peace of Augsburg</a> in 1555, membership in the Order was open to Protestants, although the majority of brothers remained Catholic.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The Teutonic Knights became tri-denominational, with Catholic, Lutheran and Reformed bailiwicks.</p>
<p>The Grand Masters, often members of the great German families (and, after 1761, members of the House of <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a>-<a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Lorraine" title="Duchy of Lorraine">Lorraine</a>), continued to preside over the Order's considerable holdings in Germany. Teutonic Knights from Germany, Austria, and Bohemia were used as battlefield commanders leading mercenaries for the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Monarchy</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe" title="Ottoman wars in Europe">Ottoman wars in Europe</a>. The military history of the Teutonic Knights ended in 1809, when <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I of France">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> ordered their dissolution and the Order lost its remaining secular holdings to Napoleon's vassals and allies.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_organisation">Medieval organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Teutonic_Order&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Medieval organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
